## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, time t, and velocity v, which is the standard second-order ODE form for (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Typical relationships combine a restoring force term depending on x, damping depending on v (often nonlinear), and optional time-dependent/periodic forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke restoring force)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven damped oscillator (cosine drive): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (phase-shifted forcing)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle model: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (nonlinear restoring force + damping)
- Duffing oscillator (softening/hardening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity)
- Duffing with periodic drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos regimes)
- Quadratic (or aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared drag-like damping)
- Nonlinear restoring with higher odd terms: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear spring)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-based self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (limit cycle via nonlinear damping)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, parametric resonance)
- LiÃ©nard-type oscillator (general form): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**4) * v - (c3 * x + c4 * x**3) (broad class capturing many nonlinear oscillators)
- Conservative potential + damping decomposition: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - c2 * v (acceleration as -dU/dx minus dissipation proxy)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force symmetry: many oscillators have odd restoring terms in x (e.g., -c*x - c*x^3), so dv_dt is often an odd function of x when centered at equilibrium.
- Conservative vs dissipative separation: conservative dynamics often appear as dv_dt depending only on x (dv_dt = -dU/dx), while any dependence on v typically signals damping or self-excitation.
- Limit-cycle signatures: terms like (c0 - x**2)*v (Van der Pol/LiÃ©nard) indicate amplitude-dependent effective damping that stabilizes oscillation amplitude.
- Self-excited oscillation from velocity nonlinearity: combinations like c1*v - c2*v**3 create negative damping at small |v| and positive damping at large |v|, yielding stable oscillations.
- Hardening/softening spring identification: the sign/magnitude of the x**3 term in dv_dt distinguishes hardening vs softening Duffing behavior and shifts resonance frequency with amplitude.
- External forcing detection: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt suggest driven oscillations; multiple harmonics (sin(c*t)+sin(2c*t)) indicate nonsinusoidal forcing.
- Parametric excitation detection: stiffness modulation patterns like -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x indicate parametric resonance behavior (energy injected via time-varying coefficient on x).
- Nonlinear drag regimes: appearance of v*Abs(v) or v**3 suggests quadratic/cubic damping typical of higher-speed regimes and produces amplitude-dependent decay rates.
- Near-equilibrium linearization: if dv_dt contains small-x approximations (sin(c*x) â‰ˆ c*x), models may transition from sinusoidal (pendulum) to linear spring behavior at small amplitude.

Key observations:
- The term `v*exp(-Abs(v))` is crucial and unique - it's not a standard polynomial, exponential, or trigonometric function
- There's no `x` dependence in GT
- There's no constant offset in GT (but candidates can have c=0)

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `v*exp(-Abs(v))` or something equivalent:

**Candidates 1-2:** Have `v**c6`, `sin(t)`, `v` terms, plus `v/(c+t)**2`. No `v*exp(-Abs(v))` term. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates 17-50:** Let me check for `exp(c*v)` terms which could potentially relate to `v*exp(-Abs(v))`:

Candidates with `exp(c*v)`: 17, 24, 26, 27, 28, 30, 34, 35, 37, 40, 45, 46, 50

For these, `exp(c*v)` with constant c cannot equal `v*exp(-Abs(v))` because `v*exp(-|v|)` is NOT an exponential function - it's a product of v and exp(-|v|). The term `exp(c*v)` alone (even with a coefficient) cannot produce the factor of `v` multiplied by the exponential, and `-Abs(v)` in the exponent makes it non-analytic at v=0.
